# Text Elements
Software Design ^4FsvUZb9

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Counting]]<<<***%%Unit 2: Visual Modeling ^PWCZStre

Software Engineering Concepts ^ETNg6aCp

Project: Whose purpose is to
develop a software system ^4AjCA6Kz

Activity: Project is composed 
of a # of activities ^mZ6OWyfR

Task: Each activity is
composed of a # of tasks
A task consumes resources
and produces a work product
Resource: are either
participants, time, or equipment 
Work Product: a system, model,
or document ^idMSAAIT

Requirements ^oYUk8LXd

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Functional Requirement]]<<<***%%Functional Requirement: an area of functionality the 
system must support (something the system must do) ^Z1fLXmI6

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Non-Functional Requirement]]<<<***%%Non-Functional Requirement: a constraint on the 
operation of the system (how it must do it)
(Ex. in x amount of time) ^Bsn1Ovc6

technique for solving a
specific problem ^u68ueLCh

directly with the system. They represent
roles that people and things play ^8upEcck7

are related by an include relationship
if one includes the other in its flow
of events ^NyToJUnp

Supplier ^x4RI6Ykv

case ^jGQ2LMsT

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Dependency Relationship]]<<<***%%Dependency: a class needs to know about another class to use

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Aggregation]]<<<***%%Aggregation:
putting objects together to make a bigger object. the parts can
sometimes exist independently of the whole or have shared
ownership ^ejygzfp0

class1 ^X97EWVr8

class2 ^4AUoKu9i

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Composition Relationship]]<<<***%%Composition:
A stronger form of aggregation. The parts have no independent
life outside the whole. Each part belongs to one and only one
whole ^ioFoaol5

class1 ^YkFAH2Of

class2 ^M5IbzvTk

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Inheritance]]<<<***%%Inheritance:
a class that is a type of another class. The child class inherits
attributes and functions from the parent ^xnUThLXl

class1 ^BUSEjomy

class2 ^gcwzOlZK

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Sequence Diagram]]<<<***%%Sequence Diagram ^u15nrLjF

used to capture the order of interactions ^vUFCi6hr

between parts of your system. 1st column: Actor who initiated,
2nd Column: Boundary Object Actor used, 3rd Column: Control
Objects that manages rest of use case. Control objects are
created at start by Boundary objects. They create the other
boundary objects. Entity objects are accessed by control and
boundary objects but the reverse cannot be true. ^wFwIp2ji

Interactions ^to5HgiOU

occurs when a participant sends a
 ^4y00sdk9

message to another. ^ynz9vSBj

Message ^ND6q5KUC

think of it as an ^nMweOCfo

event that is passed from a message caller to
get the message receiver to do something ^WUrmKaTu

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Synchronous Message]]<<<***%%Synchronous Message ^O0aBs6nA

a message where the  ^47EWqTQg

message caller waits for the message receiver
to return from the message invocation ^h3BqVj42

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Asynchronous Message]]<<<***%%Asynchronous Message ^zexMZ7gq

a message where the ^yZPLSTC9

caller does not wait for the message return
before carrying on ^39nSEoYX

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Sequence Fragment]]<<<***%%Sequence Fragment ^2pLqTN3M

is used for interactions ^G9TiJZNH

that we want to use elsewhere ^WvcYYxan

%%***>>>text element-link:[[SoftwareEngineering/SEYr2/Activity Diagram]]<<<***%%Activity Diagram ^1hgTbWjz

specifies how ^vXAcTb1X

the system will accomplish it's
goals. Think Flow Chart ^CeYz4mHK

%%***>>>text element-link:[[UML State Machine]]<<<***%%UML State Machine ^GkZCpeHn

models the ^ZUFKRB4d

system as a Finite State
Machine. shows states and
transitions resulting from a event ^8pbyhj2S

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Object Design Modeling]]<<<***%%Unit 5: Object Design Modeling ^3iNDadSI

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Entity Objects]]<<<***%%Entity Objects ^7N23MKSx

represent persistent ^9jiacKyn

information used by the system
(persistent database objects) ^WsuQVasS

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Boundary Objects]]<<<***%%Boundary Objects ^WDaU8EHn

represent the interaction ^T8PbAIh6

between the user and the system. (the user
interface). collects information from the actor ^7FsyAetC

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Control Objects]]<<<***%%Control Objects ^nklx9lZm

represent the ^aAOgRVkB

control tasks performed by the system. ^vgJWbZij

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Reuse Patterns]]<<<***%%Unit 6: Reuse Patterns ^8rYhmMUR

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Design Pattern]]<<<***%%Design Pattern ^NgoKADMy

patterns capture proven solutions ^Ht4blZrc

to recurring design problems. ^oPuVocCH

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Adapter Pattern]]<<<***%%Adapter Pattern ^9vBQpTwJ

convert ^rJH10LVH

the interface of a class into
an interface clients can use ^OMpqVRGr

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Composite Pattern]]<<<***%%Composite Pattern ^5P3nieGh

compose objects into
tree structures. lets
clients treat
individual objects and
compositions of objs
uniformly ^8EA0Btt6

%%***>>>text element-link:[[State Pattern]]<<<***%%State Pattern ^83aiid3l

when objects ^qcdQL32D

have a complicated life cycle
we allow an object to alter
it's behavior when it's internal 
state changes. The Object will 
also appear to change it's 
class (each state is a class) ^cYnroJRF

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Observer Pattern]]<<<***%%Observer Pattern ^rEve8E2g

here we define a one to
many dependency between
objects so that when one 
object changes state, all
 ^M4A9I1RS

it's dependents are notified and
can be updated. a change in
state is reflected in another
object without being tightly coupled ^a7NabE3w

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Mediator Pattern]]<<<***%%Mediator Pattern ^vDf02rhg

define an object that ^FwRkh1fT

encapsulates how a set of objects interact ^hIvat8Xb

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Singleton Pattern]]<<<***%%Singleton Pattern ^VRznrZV3

ensures that only
  ^j66YxWHL

one instance of a class is created ^XbhZWYe7

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Strategy Pattern]]<<<***%%Strategy Pattern ^xZtaYdsm

defines a set ^CMqtpkLI

of algorithms that can be used
interchangeably. Using the best
one for the desired task. ^1HJr20Lz

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Proxy Pattern]]<<<***%%Proxy Pattern ^yGS3tpT4

provide a placeholder ^9H4tYdK7

for another object to control
access to it ^Y2YBI1lQ

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Chain of Responsibility Pattern]]<<<***%%Chain of 
Responsibility 
Pattern ^zkGXVHjm

chains processing
elements and
passes any request
messages from  ^ti2WbB9O

object to object until it reaches
an object capable of handling the
request (singly linked list) ^JAyOt9vp

%%***>>>text element-link:[[Decorator Pattern]]<<<***%%Decorator Pattern ^UcQpXcra

attach additional
  responsibilities and
  behaviors to an
  object dynamically 
  (at runtime) ^SajWpjr5
